**Time:** 2026-03-21T07:07:31.287Z

**Tool Calls:** 0

### Text Exchange - 2026-03-21 07:07:31 UTC [08:07:31 CEST]

**Assistant Response:** Now I see the issue clearly. The `openMarkdown` in `navigationSlice.ts` wraps ANY path in `http://localhost:8080/` — so when an observation references a file like `hooks.md` (without the `knowledge-management/` prefix), it becomes `http://localhost:8080/hooks.md`, which hits the SPA catch-all and returns HTML.

The fix: the `openMarkdown` action needs to route non-prefixed `.md` files to `knowledge-management/` or at minimum, the NodeDetails path normalization needs to be smarter.

Let me also l...

**Type:** Text-only exchange (no tool calls)

## Prompt Set (ps_1774077011214)

**Time:** 2026-03-21T07:10:11.214Z
**Duration:** 0ms
**Tool Calls:** 0

### Text Exchange - 2026-03-21 07:10:11 UTC [08:10:11 CEST]

**Assistant Response:** The problem is clear at lines 912-913: `findBestParent` returns `null` when no parent matches by name substring. And at line 1405, unlinked entities are left without relations, creating orphans.

The comment says "avoids flower pattern" — meaning they intentionally don't fall back to the root "Coding" node. But this creates the worse problem of unconnected nodes.

The fix: fall back to "Coding" project when no specific parent is found. A connected "flower" is better than disconnected orphans:


**Type:** Text-only exchange (no tool calls)

---

Sent:', done, 'Failed:', failed);\n    return;\n  }\n  const r = batch[idx];\n  const postData = JSON.stringify(r);\n  const req = http.request({\n    hostname: 'localhost', port: 8080, path: '/api/relations',\n    method: 'POST',\n    headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json', 'Content-Length': Buffer.byteLength(postData) }\n  }, (res) => {\n    let body = '';\n    res.on('data', d => body += d);\n    res.on('end', () => {\n      if (res.statusCode === 200 || res.statusCode === 201) done++;\n      else { failed++; if (failed <= 3) console.log('Failed:', r.from, '->', r.to, body.substring(0, 100)); }\n      sendNext(idx + 1);\n    });\n  });\n  req.on('error', () => { failed++; sendNext(idx + 1); });\n  req.write(postData);\n  req.end();\n}\nconsole.log('Sending', batch.length, 'relations to GraphDB...');\nsendNext(0);\n\" 2>&1",

### Text Exchange - 2026-03-21 07:28:11 UTC [08:28:11 CEST]

**Assistant Response:** It returns the SPA catch-all HTML. So the route isn't matching because Express normalizes the URL before matching. The `../../` in the URL gets resolved by Express before reaching our handler, so the route doesn't match `/repo-file/*`. This means the traversal protection is actually working via Express's own URL normalization — the request never reaches our handler, it falls through to the SPA catch-all.

This is acceptable security — the path traversal attempt returns the SPA HTML (not sensitiv...
